## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics: oscillations and damping/forcing)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is an acceleration specified as a first-order ODE dv/dt = f(t, v), which is typical in reduced models of nonlinear oscillators where velocity-dependent damping, self-excitation, and time-periodic forcing/parameter modulation dominate. With only (t, v) available, likely structures include linear/nonlinear drag terms in v plus periodic or transient forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear relaxation (viscous damping): dv_dt = c0 * v (exponential growth/decay of velocity depending on sign of c0)
- Constant acceleration / bias: dv_dt = c0 (uniform forcing or constant bias in acceleration)
- Harmonic forcing (velocity equation with external periodic drive): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) (pure time-periodic forcing)
- Damped + driven (linear drag + periodic drive): dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3) (viscous damping with external sinusoidal forcing)
- Quadratic drag (aerodynamic-like): dv_dt = c0 * v * Abs(v) (damping magnitude grows ~v^2 with sign opposing motion when c0 < 0)
- Cubic (Rayleigh-type) nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (nonlinear dissipation; can stabilize/limit large velocities if c1 < 0)
- Self-excited (Rayleigh/Van-der-Pol-like in v-only form): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * v**2) * v (negative damping at small |v| and positive at large |v| for appropriate signs → limit-cycle tendency)
- Dry/Coulomb friction (smoothed): dv_dt = c0 * tanh(c1 * v) (approximately constant-magnitude opposing acceleration for large |v|)
- Parametrically modulated damping: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3)) * v (time-periodic damping/energy injection)
- Duffing-like effective nonlinearity in velocity equation (empirical): dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (combined nonlinear drag and harmonic forcing)
- Transient/impulsive forcing (Gaussian pulse): dv_dt = c0 * exp(-c1 * (t - c2)**2) + c3 * v (kick-like forcing plus linear drag)
- Multi-tone drive (beating/resonance proxy): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) + c4 * v (superposed excitations with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Velocity-proportional term (c*v) indicates viscous damping or linear instability (sign decides dissipation vs pumping).
- Odd nonlinearities in v (c*v**3, (c0+c1*v**2)*v) typically represent amplitude-dependent damping/self-excitation and can create effective limiting behavior.
- Terms like v*Abs(v) indicate quadratic drag where dissipation increases strongly with speed and is insensitive to the sign beyond direction.
- tanh(c*v) suggests dry friction/velocity saturation of friction force (approaches constant magnitude at large |v|).
- Pure sin/cos in t indicates externally driven oscillations; phase shifts ( + c2 ) represent initial phase/forcing alignment.
- Time-periodic coefficients multiplying v ( (c0+c1*cos(...))*v ) indicate parametric modulation (e.g., periodically varying damping or energy injection).
- Gaussian-in-time forcing exp(-c*(t-c0)^2) indicates localized impulses/kicks or transient disturbances rather than steady driving.
- Sum of nearby-frequency sinusoids in t suggests beating/envelope phenomena in the response even in a first-order velocity model.

I need to determine if any candidate can be made mathematically equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT:** `F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v) - c0*beta*v = 0.106257*sin(t) - 0.484397*sin(v) - 0.968794*v`

The GT has three basis functions: `sin(t)`, `sin(v)`, and `v`.

Let me analyze the key structural requirement: the GT contains `sin(v)` — a sine function of the variable `v`. This is a critical basis function that many candidates lack.

**Candidates with only polynomial terms in v (like v, v³) plus trig functions of t:**
Candidates 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 10, 12, 13, 14, 15, 16, 17, 20, 21, 25, 27, 28, 31, 32, 34, 35, 36, 38, 39, 41, 42, 43, 44, 45, 46, 47, 49, 50, 51, 52, 53, 54 — these cannot match because `sin(v)` cannot be represented by polynomials in `v`.

**Candidates with tanh(v):** 8, 9, 30, 33, 37, 48 — `tanh` is not equivalent to `sin(v) + linear(v)` for all v.

**Candidates with sigmoid-like terms:** 26, 40 — `1/(c*exp(v)+1)` is not `sin(v)`.

**Candidate 22:** `c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + c3*sin(c4*v + c5) + c6*exp(c7*(c8 + t)²)`
Set c6=0 to eliminate the exponential. Then: `c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + c3*sin(c4*v + c5)`.
Expand: `c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + c3*[sin(c4*v)cos(c5) + cos(c4*v)sin(c5)]`
GT needs: `0.106257*sin(t) - 0.484397*sin(v) - 0.968794*v`
This gives `sin(t)` and `sin(v)` terms but NO linear `v` term. Cannot match.

**Candidate 23:** `c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + c3*sin(c4*v + c5)`
Same issue — no linear `v` term. Cannot match.

**Candidate 24:** `c0*v + c1 + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*cos(c6*t + c7)`
Set c1=0. Expand: `c0*v + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*cos(c6*t + c7)`
= `c0*v + c2*[sin(c3*v)cos(c4) + cos(c3*v)sin(c4)] + c5*cos(c6*t + c7)`

Set c3=1, c4=0: `c0*v + c2*sin(v) + c5*cos(c6*t + c7)`
Set c6=1, c7=π/2: `c5*cos(t + π/2) = -c5*sin(t)`

So: `c0*v + c2*sin(v) - c5*sin(t)`
Set c0 = -0.968794, c2 = -0.484397, c5 = -0.106257.

This gives: `-0.968794*v - 0.484397*sin(v) + 0.106257*sin(t)` ✓

**This matches the GT exactly!**

**Candidate 19:** `c0*v + c1*v³ + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*cos(c6*t + c7)`
Set c1=0, c3=1, c4=0: `c0*v + c2*sin(v) + c5*cos(c6*t + c7)`
Set c6=1, c7=π/2: same as above. **Also matches!**

**Candidate 29:** `c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + c3*sin(c4*v + c5) + c6*t/(c7*t + c8) + c9/(c7*t + c8)`
Set c6=0, c9=0 to eliminate rational terms. Then same as Candidate 23 — no linear v. Cannot match.

**Candidate 11:** Has `sin(c6*log(c7*Abs(c8*v) + 1) + c9)` — not `sin(v)`.

**Candidate 18:** `c0*v + c1 + c2*v^c3 + c4*cos(c5*t + c6)` — no `sin(v)`.

So **Candidates 19 and 24** match.
